<div id="review_2168855906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2168855906" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2168855906?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781409083191" href="/book/show/13482358-house-of-chains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2168855906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11411015154920978067"><b>
  <i>Shadow is ever besieged, for that is its nature. Whilst darkness devours, and light steals. And so one sees shadow ever retreat to hidden places, only to return in the wake of the war between dark and light.</i>
</b><br/><br/>This series is far becoming one of my favourite series, there is absolutely nothing I don’t like about this series, the world is amazing, the cultures, races, religion, gods etc. are so unique, I seriously have not seen anything like this before. Just like its predecessors this book has l</span>
  <span id="freeText11411015154920978067" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Shadow is ever besieged, for that is its nature. Whilst darkness devours, and light steals. And so one sees shadow ever retreat to hidden places, only to return in the wake of the war between dark and light.</i>
</b><br /><br />This series is far becoming one of my favourite series, there is absolutely nothing I don’t like about this series, the world is amazing, the cultures, races, religion, gods etc. are so unique, I seriously have not seen anything like this before. Just like its predecessors this book has lots of well depicted battles, enough romance, friendship and betrayal, the worst I’ve seen in the series so far. We get to know the history of the Whirlwind goddess, a lot about the T’lan Imass, Tiste Edur, Tiste Liason and more.<br /><br /><u>World building and Writing</u><br />I adore the Malazan world, the author is a genius, the depictions are perfect, most of the book took place in Raruku desert, the other locations include Warrens, and cities and town we’ve yet to see in the previous books, still the author gave an in-depth descriptions of all. The writing also is perfect, third person multiple POVs as usual.<br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br />Well its Malazan, lots of new characters mixed with the old ones, some of my favourites in this book are:<br /><br /><b>Karsa Orlong</b> a very grey character, I was indifferent towards him at first but that changed, I don’t agree with lots of his decisions but I totally understand. He started off as arrogant, brutal, bloodthirsty, ignorant among other things, but that changed, he made great friends and travelled a lot, that changed his world view for the better. His friendship with Torvald Nom is one of my favourite things about the book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>'Shall we pay a visit?' Torvald asked.<br />'Yes,' Karsa replied, walking towards the footpath.<br />The Daru quickly moved up beside him. 'No trophies, though, right?'<br />Shrugging, the Teblor said, 'That depends on how we are received.'<br />'Strangers on a desolate beach, one of them a giant with a sword almost as tall as me. In the dead of night. Pounding on the door. If we're met with open arms, Karsa, it will be a miracle.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Onrack the Broken</b> is a T’lan Imass, but lacks their indifferent attitude, he is instead sympathetic and kind, just like Tool, He befriended <b> Trull Sengur</b> a Tiste Edur, I really enjoyed their part in the book, and what they discovered, can’t mention cause of spoilers.<br /><br /><b>Crokus and Apsalar</b> have a weird relationship with Cotillion, mainly cause of what he did to Apsalar, his other reason are still unknown to me, so they went on another adventure that was filled with battles and near death situations, I love these two so much, the only teenagers in this whole Malazan series, apart from Felisin. I like that they act so mature.<br /><br />Apsalar to Cotillion<br /><b>
  <i>'You don't seem much like a god at all, Cotillion.'<br />'I'm not a god in the traditional fashion, I am a patron. Patrons have responsibilities. Granted, I rarely have the opportunity to exercise them.'</i>
</b><br /><br /><b> Felisin</b> is now Sha’ik reborn, and not just by name, I suddenly miss the old her, I wish she didn’t accept to be Sha’ik, the rebellion already had a bad foundation, due to what Korbolo Dom did in DhG, she still has her formal flaw, she never listens, but she is more likable here.<br /><br /><b>L’oric</b> is one of the High Mages of the rebellion and the only one I like, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ He is a Tiste Liason, the son of Osric, Osric is the first son of light and the Lord of Light. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He is so kind and noble.<br /><br /><b>Kalam Mekhar</b> my favourite assassin, well he can stay away from a fight can he? After the incidents of DhG, I thought he won’t be involved again but no, he is back and more badass than ever.<br /><br /><b> Strings</b> formally known as Fiddler, well he reenlisted as he said in DhG, his new Company and Squad are as crazy as the Bridge Burners, even though most are recruits, some old ones like Gesler, Stormy and Truth, the battle plan and the battle itself is always fun to read from his POV.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Then she'd spend half the night cleaning her pincers and licking her lips—'<br />'Lips?' Smiles asked from behind the three men. 'What lips? Scorpions don't have lips—'<br />'What do you know?' Bottle shot back. 'You won't even get close—'<br />'When I get close to a scorpion I kill it. Which is what any sane person would do.'<br />'Sane?' the mage retorted. 'You pick them up and start pulling things off! Tail, pincers, legs – I ain't seen nothing so cruel in my life!'<br />'Well, ain't that close enough to see if it's got lips?'<br />'Where's it all go, I wonder?' Tarr muttered.<br />Bottle nodded. 'I know, it's amazing. She's so tiny ...'<br />'That's our secret,' Strings said quietly.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Cotillion</b> my favourite god, He is so kind for a god, also considerate, the rest gods are so selfish and indifferent to humans as long as they are not using them, but Cotillion is not like that, and for that I love him. Well he is a Patron god of Assassins, so being a badass is in the job description.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>And a fifth figure was among the four Edur sorcerers now, grey-clad, gloved, face hidden in a rough hood. In its hands, a rope, that seemed to writhe with a life of its own. Cutter saw it snap out to strike a sorcerer in one eye, and when the rope whipped back out, a stream of blood and minced brains followed. The sorcerer's magic winked out and the Edur toppled.<br />The rope was too fast to follow, as its wielder moved among the three remaining mages, but in its twisting wake a head tumbled from shoulders, intestines spilled out from a gaping rip, and whatever felled the last sorcerer happened in a blur that left no obvious result, except that the Edur was dead before he hit the ground.</i>
</b><br /><br />In case you are still wondering, that was Cotillion.<br /><br />Other characters I adore include Heboric, Pearl, Lastori, Keneb, Gamet, Temul, Nil and Nether, Felisin younger, the whole of Strings squad, Leoman and a host of others.<br /><br />Pearl and Lastori<br /><b>
  <i>'What do you make of that night sky, Pearl? I do not recognize the constellations... nor have I ever before seen those glowing swirls in any night sky I've looked at.'<br />He grunted. 'That's a foreign sky – as foreign as can be. A hole leading into alien realms, countless strange worlds filled with creatures unimaginable—'<br />'You really don't know, do you?'<br />'Of course I don't!' he snapped.<br />'Then why didn't you just say so?'</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>Plot</u><br />The first third quarter if the book focus on Karsa Orlong and his backstory, after that the story continued from where it ended in DhG and MoI, so lots of battle and desert living. Tavore is now the new adjunct, before I forgot, I loathe her more than the soldiers, she is so annoying, Sha’ik and her people are leading the rebellion, The realm of shadows and its rulers interfere for very important reasons this time. The T’lan Imass are still on their hunt for tyrants, these time renegades, throw the Tiste Edur, Andii and Liason in the mix, oh they are jaghut in this also and the Eres an elder race, that basically sum up the whole book without spoilers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11411015154920978067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_852568777" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852568777" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28602001-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438967931p2/28602001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/852568777?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/28602001-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2966155456949398035">It horrifies me a little but I'm reducing my star rating from 5 to 4 on this one. While it ends with an epic battle and has some excellent character moments, I still skipped the whole first quarter of Karsa. Yes, he shows some serious growth through the book and his answer to Bidithal has my full appreciation, but otherwise he gets on my last nerve.<br/><br/>One of the things that occurred to me because of this was how much more rereaders get from this series. At this point, everyone should have realised </span>
  <span id="freeText2966155456949398035" style="display:none">It horrifies me a little but I'm reducing my star rating from 5 to 4 on this one. While it ends with an epic battle and has some excellent character moments, I still skipped the whole first quarter of Karsa. Yes, he shows some serious growth through the book and his answer to Bidithal has my full appreciation, but otherwise he gets on my last nerve.<br /><br />One of the things that occurred to me because of this was how much more rereaders get from this series. At this point, everyone should have realised that nobody is safe, but also that each character introduction could lead to an ever deepening relationship over pages or books...or they could be gone in the next paragraph. It works for me because I can skip Karsa's origin story and jump in when he meets Keeper, where it starts to get interesting. It also means that each new meeting resonates with our emotional responses to past and future actions in a way that newbies can't yet get. It's the same for any book, I suppose, but I feel it in this series more than any other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2966155456949398035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText16031694743037895808" style="display:none">Re-Read:<br /><br />The first time through this was the weakest of the ten books for me. Although the ending still lacked the convergence power in the endings of all the other books in the series I found so many hidden breadcrumbs I missed the first time around. So many poetic moments that had more power this time around. I had forgotten, missed or misinterpreted a lot that first times. These tomes are just so vast with so much going on the sensory overload the first time takes its toll. Being able to break apart the story and knowing what's important was so fulfilling. <br /><br />This is also the book when you come to realize just how compassionate a character Cotillion is. The transformation of Karsa is even more amazing and that opening quarter of the book where it's all Karsa not nearly the slog it was the first time around. I remember the relief the first time around when I finally read the word Malazan in this book for the first time. <br /><br />Looking forward to the rest of my re-read. <br /><br />Original:<br /><br />While still a tremendous book it wasn't in the realm of greatness that are DHG or MOI and not on par with GOTM. The first few chapters with Karsa probably could have been a bit shorter. The ending while another great convergence I had issues with how some of them went down. Still when compared with everything else out there this series stands alone as truly epic.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1954433442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1836171466298745923">Once I get to the end of one of these books it feels like this huge accomplishment. Mostly because they are really so very dense and maybe it is close to 1000 pages but it seems like so much more.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437071947i/15535362._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='276' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It took a lot to get to where we were going in this book. Mainly the overall arc is that Tevore and the Malazan’s are going to march into the desert to fare Sharik and her appocolyptic sands. So that is where the various lines all converge by the end of the story. It took a long time to get there and at</span>
  <span id="freeText1836171466298745923" style="display:none">Once I get to the end of one of these books it feels like this huge accomplishment. Mostly because they are really so very dense and maybe it is close to 1000 pages but it seems like so much more.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437071947i/15535362._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="276" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It took a lot to get to where we were going in this book. Mainly the overall arc is that Tevore and the Malazan’s are going to march into the desert to fare Sharik and her appocolyptic sands. So that is where the various lines all converge by the end of the story. It took a long time to get there and at the end I will say that again most of my feelings are bittersweet. At least this one didn’t gut my insides out like the previous two books but again there seems to be no such thing as a happy ending when you are in the world of the Malazans.<br><br>I’m really never sure where the book is going to take me and this one again starts off with a culture and people that we don’t really seem to know. <b>Karsa Orlong how I hated you</b>. This started as a really difficult read because I completely hated Karsa and his cultural ways. It was difficult to real all of Book I since it was just about him and his beginnings to where we left off in Deathhouse Gates. The good news is that even though I still don’t like him per say I was rooting for him later in the book. His character went through a lot of changes so by the end of this book I grew to enjoy his arc and I have high hopes for him.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“You have learned much, Karsa Orlong."<br>"I have, T'lan Imass. As you shall witness.”</i>
</blockquote><br>The good news about travelling with Tevore and the Malazans is that we get to be with what is left of the Bridgeburners, Coltain’s wounded that were saved and some of the other wiccan clans. I don’t really like Tevore if only for what she was prepared to do to her sister. So while she isn’t my favorite I did love being with Strings a.k.a. Fiddler and some other all stars from the prior books.<br><br>Sharik, Heboric, Felisin and a slew of others had an strange and interesting tale. I will say that while Sharik wasn’t my favorite I did like Heboric and Felisin the younger quite a bit. Heboric’s change in this was actually one of my favorite parts since I really did want the once priest to find purpose again and it seems that maybe another god saw something in him too. <b>But the most memorable point driven home again was that if in a fantasy world of any kind never drink the tea,</b> it doesn’t go well fore anyone. Just ask Alice, Nynaeve, Egwene or the ever murderous Marquel. <br><br>There is some stuff with Apsalar and Crocus but they didn’t get a lot of time and in the end I didn’t really understand what happened between them. But the crazy dude who is a priest for Shadowthrone in middle of the desert and his many spidered wife are hilarious. So I did enjoy when they ended up there.<br><br>There is the big buildup going into the end and then it sort of fizzled out when we were supposed to get a big battle. I know that SE did it like that on purpose but still I guess I just wanted a bigger battle sequence after all that time getting to it. Don’t get me wrong there is still some very cool stuff that happens and I especially liked what happened to the Dog Killers but I wanted Tevore and Sharik’s story line to end a little differently I guess.<br><br>One of the more followable books in the series for me. But between warrens, gods, ascendants and races it is so hard to keep track of everything.</span>

<div id="review_313279437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313279437" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313279437?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313279437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14854364339809083744">This was another fantastic 5 star instalment in the Malazan Book of the Fallen saga. Just like with the previous books Steven Erikson did a great job of juggling a massive cast of characters and ongoing plot arcs before pulling them all together for an explosive and exciting conclusion. <br/><br/>We were back in Raraku for the battle between Tavore, and her Malazan legions, and Shai'k, and her army of the apocalypse. A battle that was far more personal than it seemed at first glance. The Gods and Ascendan</span>
  <span id="freeText14854364339809083744" style="display:none">This was another fantastic 5 star instalment in the Malazan Book of the Fallen saga. Just like with the previous books Steven Erikson did a great job of juggling a massive cast of characters and ongoing plot arcs before pulling them all together for an explosive and exciting conclusion. <br /><br />We were back in Raraku for the battle between Tavore, and her Malazan legions, and Shai'k, and her army of the apocalypse. A battle that was far more personal than it seemed at first glance. The Gods and Ascendants in the Malazan world are not a quiet bunch and they had their own games to play. The House of Chains has been sanctified and has begun a full blown assault on the other Houses. It all made for an exciting, interesting, and engaging read.<br /><br />We had a massive cast of characters and the true measure of Erikson's skill as a writer was shown as pretty much all of them proved interesting and memorable. There was not a single dull POV segment! The star of House of Chains was undoubtedly Karsa Orlong. He was not easy to like in the early stages but showed great development as the story progressed and his journey was always a gripping one. This series has always had great duos and we got two more here in the shape of Pearl and Lostara and Trull Senger and Onrack. We also got to enjoy the continued stories of a bunch of old favourite characters like Kallam, Fiddler, Crokus, Felsin, and Heboric. <br /><br />In a deep world of complex plots, intense action, and cool magic I still firmly believe it is the dialogue between the characters which makes this series so fantastic. It is always amusing and engaging.<br /><br />All in all I loved this latest Malazan book and cannot wait for the next one!<br /><br />Rating: 5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: This is the first book where Michael Page has taken over narration duties from the excellent Ralph Lister. Page is a good narrator and did an good job, but I'm still not super happy with the change as consistency of character interpretation really is the key when it comes to audiobook series. I just wish production companies and authors would keep this in mind! <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14854364339809083744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1980615587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1980615587" />
    <a title="Sade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16037420-sade"><img alt="Sade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605390492p2/16037420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1980615587?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sade" href="/user/show/16037420-sade">Sade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1980615587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5750766704854456804"><blockquote>
  <b>"Hatred is a most pernicious weed, finding root in any kind of soil. It feeds on itself"<br/>-Torvald Nom</b>
</blockquote><br/>It's almost funny that what i feel is the general theme for this book in this series is perfectly captured by a minor character in the book. Like all stories in the malazan series, there is the general sense that doing justice to it in my reviews might not always be possible. So here goes nothing.<br/> <br/>Can i just say before i delve into characters that totally wowed me that Book 4 reminded me eeril</span>
  <span id="freeText5750766704854456804" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>"Hatred is a most pernicious weed, finding root in any kind of soil. It feeds on itself"<br />-Torvald Nom</b>
</blockquote><br />It's almost funny that what i feel is the general theme for this book in this series is perfectly captured by a minor character in the book. Like all stories in the malazan series, there is the general sense that doing justice to it in my reviews might not always be possible. So here goes nothing.<br /> <br />Can i just say before i delve into characters that totally wowed me that Book 4 reminded me eerily of Gardens of the Moon. In that it's not a finished picture, threads are being woven in patterns that aren't really clear for the most part. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Cotillion:</b>
</u><br /><b>
  <blockquote>To be a god is to know the burdens of believers. Did you protect? You did not. Did you offer comfort, solace? Were you possessed of compassion? Even pity?<br />- Karsa</blockquote>
</b><br />There is a general understanding among majority of the mortal characters in the Malazan world that gods are not to be trusted. There is essentially the idea that the gods take and give nothing back. and that's why it was absolutely breath taking to see an element of dare i say kindness in Cotillion.. I absolutely loved this side of the patron god of assasins and also that rope.. hot damn!!! definitely would not want to get in a fight with him.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Karsa:</b>
</u><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[WITNESS!!!!!!!! everyone's favourite Toblaki. Ahhh what to say...I still think Karsa is way too arrogant but then again, without his arrogance i guess he wouldn't be what he is. I suppose the only reason his arrogance doesn't chafe as it did in the beginning is because it's tempered with wisdom (Bairoth Delum you finally got through). His redemption was truly beautiful<br /><b><blockquote>"My loyalty was misplaced. I served only glory. Words, my friends. And words can wear false nobility. Disguising brutal truths. The words of the past, that so clothed the Teblor in a hero's garb- this is what i served. While the true glory was before me. Beside me. You, Delum Thord. And you, Bairoth Gild"</blockquote></b><br />I almost think the crippled god is rolling in anger whereever he is for the wild card he picked for a knight.. Now that i think about it, Karsa is definitely a rougher version of Paran now.. No god is pushing those two about for any reason.<br /><b><blockquote>"When i began this journey, I was young. I believed in one thing. I believed in glory. I know now...that glory is is nothing. Nothing. This is what i now understand...The same cannot be said for mercy"</blockquote></b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />WITNESSS!!!! Lol<br /><br /><u>
  <b>T'Lan Imass:</b>
</u> For me the T'lan Imass were definitely one of the biggest shockers. I think because for the most part, at least up to this book, we had only interacted mainly with Tool and he seemed somewhat reasonable but i think in this book we actually see the T'lan Imass for what they really are and it's not pretty. I think at this stage of the book, you begin to wonder was the ritual really, really a good thing?? Maybe Kilava had a point. I think centuries of undead living has rightly left the moral compass of the T'lan Imass skewered.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Felisin/Whirlwind Goddess</b>
</u>: <b>
  <blockquote>"Vengence is a wasted emotion, yet i have let it consume me. I gave it like a gift to the goddess"</blockquote>
</b> ahh Felisin.. This was definitely a character i felt sorry for when i first met but that quickly melted away. I suppose all the anger she felt was legitimate but i couldn't help feeling that she took it too far making her succeptible to the whims of the whirlwind goddess <b>(now that was one crazy goddess)</b><br />At the end of this book though, i could only commiserate with Felisin. She had basically walked into the goddess's arms blinded with vengence and there was no coming back from that. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At the end of it all, Felisin end was heartbreaking <b><blockquote>"I just wanted to know, Tavore, why you did it. And why you did not love me, when i loved you. I- I think that's what i wanted to know"</blockquote></b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> SOB******<br /><br />All in all this was an amazing read especially when you realise it basically sets the stage for more epic things to come, i mean what's L'Oric up to exactly? and hello Minala?? What's up with her?? Who's traveler? Do we get shadowthrone's secrets?? what's the rope really up to like really??? well you get what i was saying about the uncompleted picture..</span>
  <a data-text-id="5750766704854456804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_190577990" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190577990" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4162390-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525386186p2/4162390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190577990?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/4162390-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4162390-lee?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190577990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17517109356811165920">I am not going to re-write my original review because it is all still relevant. The only thing I would add, is that it is even better second time round. But since I was already on five stars there is nothing to improve.<br/><br/><b>Story: 4/5</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>1: Being Vague, rambling plot with no little believable storyline<br/>5: Ripping yarn, clever, thought provoking</i>
</blockquote><br/>Without doubt my favourite in the series so far. If you have read the previous three and wondering whether to start number four. Stop reading this and go read H</span>
  <span id="freeText17517109356811165920" style="display:none">I am not going to re-write my original review because it is all still relevant. The only thing I would add, is that it is even better second time round. But since I was already on five stars there is nothing to improve.<br /><br /><b>Story: 4/5</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1: Being Vague, rambling plot with no little believable storyline<br />5: Ripping yarn, clever, thought provoking</i>
</blockquote><br />Without doubt my favourite in the series so far. If you have read the previous three and wondering whether to start number four. Stop reading this and go read House of Chains.<br />So the overall rating is a 5/5, but the story I am giving ⅘, but for no other reason than, by itself it is a great book, if you have read the series, then its a awesome book. <br />The story brings together so many threads from Deadhouse and Memories of Ice. I still find it amazing that Erikson’s story is so freaking large, that it took nearly three books to tell a story that was all happening at the same time. His attention to detail is amazing, and often tells part of a story that links back to something you read in book 2 and you’re suddenly remembering back to Deadhouse days. Certainly the first time I have been reading a book in mid series and thought “I’d love to go back and start again now I know all this”. Maybe the story is just to big to be told?<br /><br />The story brings together the Malazan Empire against the Apocalypse army of the whirlwind goddess, which has one of the strangest final battles I have ever read. Seriously, three books leading up to the final battle and it ends like that? Wow! Brave, Mr Erikson, brave. It’s what I like about the story, it can be unexpected.<br /><br />As usual there are lots of stories within the main story, but I think the story of the Thelomen Toblakai is powerfully written and not only creates a wonderful character but has me excited about the story in the future.<br /><br /><b>Characters: 5 /5</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1: Unrealistic/unbelievable. Feel nothing for these characters<br />5: Fully engaged with the characters, believable. Researched.</i>
</blockquote><br />When ever I start a new one of these Malazan books, I always look at the character list at the start to see if I actually know anyone from previous books. On reading this one, I must admit I was a little daunted by having to learn another thirty odd characters. But Erikson continues to bring brilliantly written roles to the story. Without doubt, you’ll see the name Karsa Orlong throughout reviews on this book, it is a hugely powerful character, not only in physical strength, but the role though-out the story. A truely terrible man, that even the gods cannot control, yet a favourite for many readers.<br />The book continues to bring wonderful relationships to the story, the Malazan army has units that really are made up of odd types, who like each other, hate each other, bicker, fight and die for each other. Erikson really catches the army/marine camaraderie well and makes the day to day stuff on a march to war entertaining. There are some characters that I am beginning to bore with, I do not feel they are developing, in fact, I am feeling cooler to them as I read on. Crokus/Cutter and Aspalar is a story, to be quite honest with you, I am done with.<br /><br /><b>Read Weight: </b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Fluffy, Light, Solid, Heavy, Struggle</i>
</blockquote><br />Heavy, if you havent read the 3 before, then it will be a struggle.<br /><br /><b>Engagement: 4 /5</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1: Not fussed about finishing<br />5: Could stay up all night</i>
</blockquote><br />Can’t give this 5, because I couldnt read it all night. It is so big, the story so large, that after 3 hours of reading, I need to put it down and sit and stare into space for a while to compile the story. I couldn’t wait to pick it up again though.<br /><br /><b>Recommend: 1-5/5</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1: Would advise you to read something else<br />5: Go read it now. It is THAT good</i>
</blockquote><br />If you had <b>not</b> read the previous books, I would advise <b>do not</b> read this. If you <b>have</b> read the previous books, I would be saying, you <b>should</b> read it now. It is <u>THAT</u> good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17517109356811165920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2422536519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2422536519" />
    <a title="Graeme Rodaughan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56397934-graeme-rodaughan"><img alt="Graeme Rodaughan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464911366p2/56397934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2422536519?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graeme Rodaughan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graeme Rodaughan" href="/user/show/56397934-graeme-rodaughan">Graeme Rodaughan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of Epic Fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=dark-fantasy-book-series">dark-fantasy-book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=heroic-fantasy">heroic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=sorcerors-magicians">sorcerors-magicians</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2422536519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4853689222196805385"><b>"Hither came <s>Conan, the Cimmerian</s> Karsa Orlong, of the Toblakai; black-haired, sullen-eyed, sword in hand, a thief, a reaver, a slayer, with gigantic melancholies and gigantic mirth, to tread the jeweled thrones of <s>the Earth</s> Genabackis under his sandaled feet."</b><br/><br/>Whoops right quote, but wrong character, hat tip to Robert E. Howard.<br/><br/>I love Erickson's ability to weave a multitude of conflicts together into a coherent and seamless whole. I am in awe of his ability to do that. Frankly, I'm just in love </span>
  <span id="freeText4853689222196805385" style="display:none"><b>"Hither came <s>Conan, the Cimmerian</s> Karsa Orlong, of the Toblakai; black-haired, sullen-eyed, sword in hand, a thief, a reaver, a slayer, with gigantic melancholies and gigantic mirth, to tread the jeweled thrones of <s>the Earth</s> Genabackis under his sandaled feet."</b><br /><br />Whoops right quote, but wrong character, hat tip to Robert E. Howard.<br /><br />I love Erickson's ability to weave a multitude of conflicts together into a coherent and seamless whole. I am in awe of his ability to do that. Frankly, I'm just in love with these "books of the Fallen," series.<br /><br />The only thing that troubled me is that sometimes his story telling can bog down into "two heads talking history while a tortoise wanders by," and those who've read this book will know the reference, well at this point the pace dragged and became - with no pun intended - tortoise like.<br /><br />As for Karsa - loved him from the start - what a majestic, charismatic character, and I look forward to finding out what happens next.<br /><br />Strongly recommend this book and the series for anyone with a passion for epic, heroic, dark, gritty fantasy. Sure it can be confusing at times, but everything comes out and explanations become clear, it just takes time.<br /><br /><b>A highly enjoyable, moving, interesting read. Strongly recommended, 5 'Conan Approves,' stars.</b></span>

<div id="review_1288639676" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288639676" />
    <a title="Molly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9077850-molly"><img alt="Molly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345305363p2/9077850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1288639676?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly" href="/user/show/9077850-molly">Molly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=steven-erikson">steven-erikson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288639676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1353205731488897877"><b>
  <i>This is an easy five.</i>
</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438948870i/15773192._SY540_.jpg' height='592' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>This is what you'd call a tardy review</b> (finished the book months ago)<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Hatred, sweet as nectar.<br/>I have walked into the abyss.<br/>I am as mad as that goddess. And this is why she chose me, for we are kindred souls... <br/>Then what is this ledge to which I still cling so desperately? Why do I persist in my belief that I can save myself? That I can return . . . find once more the place where madness cannot be found, where confusion does not exist.<br/>The place ... of childhood.”</i>
</b> <br/><br/>Man</span>
  <span id="freeText1353205731488897877" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>This is an easy five.</i>
</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438948870i/15773192._SY540_.jpg" height="592" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This is what you'd call a tardy review</b> (finished the book months ago)<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“Hatred, sweet as nectar.<br>I have walked into the abyss.<br>I am as mad as that goddess. And this is why she chose me, for we are kindred souls... <br>Then what is this ledge to which I still cling so desperately? Why do I persist in my belief that I can save myself? That I can return . . . find once more the place where madness cannot be found, where confusion does not exist.<br>The place ... of childhood.”</i>
</b> <br><br>Many readers find <i>House of Chains</i> to be of inferior quality and less engaging then the first three (or at least compared to <i>Deadhouse Gates</i> and <i>Memories of Ice</i>). Others complain they were cheated of an expected major, epic battle (that didn't come), and there are those that hated <i>Karsa</i> as a character at the beginning of the book, and complained about it till the end missing the rest of the story. (Or dropped the book eighty pages in! Who are you people?) Well, their loss.<br><br><b>Inferior quality? Oh. Come. On.</b> I don't want to comment on that. We've been reading different books obviously.<br><br><b>Epic battle missing? I can understand that .... up to a point.</b> The so much anticipated clash between the <i>Malazan</i> forces and the <i>Whirlwind</i> rebels would have diminished the impact of that long awaited, tragic face-off between <b>Adjunct Tavore and her sister Felisin</b> (now 'Sha'ik Reborn'). Epic battles are great, and I don't know if anyone does them better than Erikson. Clashes of armies, sieges of cities or those almost "nuclear" sorcerous attacks of the <i>mage cadre</i> ... and the devastation that follows them are always breathtaking, but very often is the small, personal, almost quiet moments like this tragic meeting of estranged sisters that hit you the hardest.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>“She was lithe, light on her feet, achingly economical. She was, for this moment, perfect.<br><i>But, for me, the blood is heavy. So heavy.</i><br>And Felisin struggled against it – that sudden, overwhelming weight. Struggled to raise her arms – unthinking of how that motion would be received.<br><i>Tavore, it’s all right—</i><br>Then something punched into her chest, a stunning blossom of cold fire piercing through flesh, bone...<br><br>Through the visor’s slit, she stared up at her sister, a figure standing behind a web of black, twisted iron wire that now rested cool over her eyes, tickling her lashes."<br>Blood.<br><i>Of course. This is how you break an unbreakable chain.<br>By dying.</i><br><br>The boot lifted from her chest. But she could still feel its weight.<br><i>Heavy. So very heavy . . .<br>Oh, Mother, look at us now.”</i></b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So .... no epic battle? It's just one of ten 900+ pages books, people! I suspect there will be battles galore, "blood to the knees" and so on. Epic fantasy doesn't have a requirement of one per book, most fantasy books I've read have only minor battles (if any). <b>Aaaaanyway, we have plenty of action in this one. Don't nitpick.</b><br><br><b>Karsa haters? Hmph...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438948870i/15773193._SY540_.jpg" height="592" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I must admit I wished for the guy to be killed for the first one hundred-ish pages. <b>Not a bundle of love and joy, Karsa Orlong</b>, but the despicable bastard grows up and grows on you as the story progresses, and I suspect he may become one of my favorites. I didn't care for him much in <i>Deadhouse Gates</i>, and when I realized that a big chunk of this book would be Karsa's backstory, I was less than thrilled ... but <b>Erikson makes you care for unexpected characters.</b><br><br>And as for those (few) readers that wished <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[for the <i>Whirlwind rebellion</i> to succeed ... I don't get them. The <i>Whirlwind Goddess</i> that possessed <i>Felisin/Sha'ik Reborn</i> was obviously insane. As for the rest of the leaders of the rebellion ... most of them were power hungry monsters. I get that the <i>Malazan Empire</i> was the invader here, but with this kind of would-be rulers and profiteers (like Bidithal or Kamist Reloe and such scum)trying to rise and lead (or use as a stepping stone for grander plans) the once divided tribes of <i>Seven Cities</i>, no way I'll be saddened with this outcome. There were a couple of decent guys there, but too few <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>A little less interesting story-line (after their initial encounter) was perhaps the one following <b>Trull Sengar and Onrack</b> ( Not badly written at all.... I was just more engaged with the rest of the characters.), though now, after finishing <i>Midnight Tides</i> as well .... <br>Trull grows on you. Slowly, yes ... ( and not in this book ) but now I'm curious what will happen to the <i>Sengar</i> brothers. Should have paid more attention while reading this book (Erikson is one of those authors that make me want to do a re-read right away. And the length of his books is no joke).<br><br><b>It's again a great book. Yes, yes .... by now I'm a full-fledged Malazan fan. Sue me.</b><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1353205731488897877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2117414265" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2117414265" />
    <a title="Veronica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7035111-veronica"><img alt="Veronica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360466651p2/7035111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2117414265?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica " href="/user/show/7035111-veronica">Veronica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117414265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3391214177742024448">One of the (many) things I appreciate about this series is, so far at least, when the author devastates his readers in one book he switches the focus in the next, allowing us to recover our equilibrium…though not completely. Never completely. And so, following the heartbreaking losses in the last book, we once again find the story lens swinging back to Seven Cities and the impending showdown between the Malazan forces under the leadership of Adjunct Tavore and Sha’ik’s army of the apocalypse. <br/><br/><b>”W</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3391214177742024448" style="display:none">One of the (many) things I appreciate about this series is, so far at least, when the author devastates his readers in one book he switches the focus in the next, allowing us to recover our equilibrium…though not completely. Never completely. And so, following the heartbreaking losses in the last book, we once again find the story lens swinging back to Seven Cities and the impending showdown between the Malazan forces under the leadership of Adjunct Tavore and Sha’ik’s army of the apocalypse. <br /><br /><b>”War needs no gods, only mortal contestants, two enemies and whatever reasons they invent in order to justify killing each other.”</b><br /><br />Along the way we get to catch up with several old friends and that was great. In fact those chapters were my favorite ones to read. Though the book’s main focus is the looming battle between Tavore and Sha’ik, which is fraught with complications, I found I was the least interested in either of those two characters. While I admit to ending the story with feelings of compassion for Sha’ik <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(Felisin the Older) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, Tavore remains a bland spot on an otherwise colorful canvas. She is lost in a crowd of memorable – for good or ill - characters. Speaking of memorable characters, a new one bursts onto the scene in this book, Karsa Orlong. In fact, Part One of the book deals entirely with him. It made for a bit of a disjointed start in my opinion. If the author was going to devote that much page time to a character, I’d have much rather it been Anomander Rake, or Coltaine, or Anomander Rake, or Whiskeyjack, or ANOMANDER RAKE. You get the picture. <br /><br />Gardens of the Moon was a great introduction to the Malazan world and Deadhouse Gates and Memories of Ice both had endings that gutted me, leaving me feeling sad for days. House of Chains, in my opinion, lacked that emotional punch to the gut. While there a few “aww” moments scattered throughout the narrative, overall this installment just didn’t move me in the way its predecessors did. And where the previous three books all raced to suspenseful, nail-biting conclusions, several parts of the denouement in this book came off as decidedly anti-climactic. This might be a case where appreciation for the book grows either with a reread or as its relevance becomes more apparent as the series progresses. Right now, it feels more like a bridge from one favorite spot to another. It’s still a worthy book, and no one can fault the author for the incredible world and history he’s creating, but it’s definitely my least favorite of the series so far. <br /><br /><b>”The future can ever promise one thing and one thing only: surprises.”</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3391214177742024448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_312980473" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312980473" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312980473?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8177008-house-of-chains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312980473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7484064131212937773">I know I’m sounding like a broken record, but yet again, my reread of <i>House of Chains</i> has been a far superior experience compared to the initial read. Part of that has to do with already knowing a lot of the characters coming in and knowing who will play major roles going forward, leaving the grey matter free to unpack the dense world building, plot, and themes. There is also the added enjoyment of discussing the book as part of a group read at The Malazan Fallen here on Goodreads. <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/85396'>http://www.go</a></span>
  <span id="freeText7484064131212937773" style="display:none">I know I’m sounding like a broken record, but yet again, my reread of <i>House of Chains</i> has been a far superior experience compared to the initial read. Part of that has to do with already knowing a lot of the characters coming in and knowing who will play major roles going forward, leaving the grey matter free to unpack the dense world building, plot, and themes. There is also the added enjoyment of discussing the book as part of a group read at The Malazan Fallen here on Goodreads. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/85396">http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/8...</a><br /><br />Erikson does something a little different this book to what he normally does. The first 4 chapters of the book comprising over 20% of the page count is devoted exclusively to a single POV character and a single story arc – where usually Erikson can have more character POV’s in a single chapter than George RR Martin has in a whole book. It was actually a refreshing change and makes the story somewhat more accessible. I have a mental graveyard somewhere in my head which was able to take a breather before the next wave of expired neurons had to pass through Hood’s Gate and on to brain cell heaven. It also makes it a lot easier to single out a character for special mention as a big chunk of this book is his story and his journey. Witness – Karsa Orlong.<br /><br />Karsa Orlong is a Teblor – Imagine a larger version of human, but not human. He is Erikson’s version(or subversion) of the “noble savage” trope. He starts out as a young warrior looking for glory through war. Glory for himself and for his people – but mostly for himself I think. He is arrogant, he is a warmonger, he is a rapist and a murderer. The beginning has him seeking a name for himself through actions so vile that one cannot possibly imagine him becoming anything other than a most reprehensible character. <br /><br />Having said that, it is Karsa who grows the most through this book, more so than any other character. Which leaves the reader with a conundrum to ponder. Does Karsa’s growth through the book absolve him of his past crimes? Should we as readers overlook his rapes and his victims. Shouldn’t we at least punish him by hating him for his crimes against women and against the world in general? If we see him any other way are we endorsing the actions he undertook at the beginning? <br /><br />Yet, Karsa is probably one of the most loved characters in Malazan fandom. Go visit any Malazan fan sight and any thread discussing Karsa will likely be overwhelmingly drooling over the badassery of Karsa Orlong. Yet at the same time if the topic of Karsa’s origins is brought up I doubt very many are willing to pass off his rapes and other crimes as ignorance or cultural anomalies. And this is why I think Karsa is such a well written character. Erikson has added to the “noble savage” trope something that is by enlarge missing – and that is the tension between the “noble” and the “savage” – or perhaps in Karsa’s case, the tension between the reprehensible and the not so reprehensible. Karsa is badass, but he remains a most savage badass.<br /><br />So far reading this review one might get the impression that this story is all about Karsa. It’s not. He is a large cog in the wheel, but he still remains one of many. This book sees us return to the desert of Raraku. Adjunct Tavore lands in <i>Seven Cities</i> with an army intent on giving the Empress’ answer to the atrocities committed against the Coltaine and the Chain of Dogs and the ten thousand Malazans crucified on Aren’s way. It is a story of two sisters leading two opposing armies. Two sisters bound in the chains of guilt and betrayal. It is the story of an insane goddess bound in chains of pain, the dead bound in chains of memory. Every House has its chains. Every house has it’s leper, it’s magi, it’s knight. And every House has those who rail against the chains.<br /><br />This story we have assassins and mages, gods and ghosts, Hounds of Shadow and dogs of war. We have Fiddler, Kalam, Quick Ben and Rock’n’Roll (That would be the Tanno Spirit song – sorry got carried away there). I could go on and roll the whole list of credits of returning cast members, but really there is only one name of the returning characters that stands out from the others and that’s <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The Bridgeburners <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />So pick this up, and keep your ear out for the Tanno Spirit Song. If you turn up the volume it would probably sound a little like this - <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dailymotion.com/video/xsxqk_black-sabbath-war-pigs_music#.UbqEZJbvh3s">http://www.dailymotion.com/video/xsxq...</a> (courtesy of Rob's theme music)<br /><br /><br />5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="7484064131212937773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2686184254" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2686184254" />
    <a title="Nina ✳The Surgebinder ✳" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30295592-nina-the-surgebinder"><img alt="Nina ✳The Surgebinder ✳" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606042377p2/30295592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2686184254?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina ✳The Surgebinder ✳" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina ✳The Surgebinder ✳" href="/user/show/30295592-nina-the-surgebinder">Nina ✳The Surgebinder ✳</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2686184254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15864985762441492080"><b> Among his people, it was a long-known truth, perhaps the only truth, that Nature fought but one eternal war. One foe. That, further, to understand this was to understand the world. Every world.<br/>Nature has but one enemy.And that is imbalance. </b><br/><br/>An insanely remarkable read, well written and intricately woven. The fourth tale of Malazan Book of The Fallen is both gripping and enticing, and I'm just quite at awe at how the structure of the story keeps changing with each installment yet we don't lose s</span>
  <span id="freeText15864985762441492080" style="display:none"><b> Among his people, it was a long-known truth, perhaps the only truth, that Nature fought but one eternal war. One foe. That, further, to understand this was to understand the world. Every world.<br />Nature has but one enemy.And that is imbalance. </b><br /><br />An insanely remarkable read, well written and intricately woven. The fourth tale of Malazan Book of The Fallen is both gripping and enticing, and I'm just quite at awe at how the structure of the story keeps changing with each installment yet we don't lose sight of the entire picture. And I just love how the book is trying represent the importance of maintaining balance in nature and the world. <br /><br /><b> Toblakai. A name of past glories, of a race of warriors who had stood alongside mortal Imass, alongside cold-miened Jaghut and demonic Forkrul Assail. A name by which Karsa Orlong was now known, as if he alone was the inheritor of elder dominators in a young, harsh world. </b><br /><br />The Thelomen Toblakai is one peculiar character and for me I still slightly have some reservations about him. He's quite a controversial character especially taking in consideration his history and background, I don't think it's something you can simply just look past. But what I appreciate most is the long way Karsa Orlong has come just to shed and get rid of his tarnished past, I think he's gone through an impressing character growth. I just love the way he vindicated Young Felisin and delivered justice to those who wronged, it's really one of favorite things about House of Chains, and the fact that SE dedicated quarter of the book to Tablakai is just wonderful.<br /><br /><b> A short while later there was a startled shout from Smiles, and Fiddler turned, in time to see two figures stride out from a warren. Despite everything, he found himself grinning. Old friends, he realized, were getting harder to find. Still, he knew them, and they were his brothers. Mortal souls of Raraku. Raraku, the land that had bound them together. Bound them all, as was now clear, beyond even death. Fiddler was unmindful of how it looked, of what the others thought, upon seeing the three men close to a single embrace. </b><br /><br />So when it comes to the Bridgeburners I can't stress how much I've grown to like, love and admire them as whole, and I think it's one of the reasons why I'm this invested in this series. And what I really appreciate about the series is the friendship between the Bridgeburners, it's not just friendship, it's something more deeper, it's feels like something that's in kinship level. And one of the things that struck me so hard is when Fiddler waa thinking to himself .... <b> Fiddler returned his gaze to the distant oasis. He narrowed his eyes, but the darkness defied him. Something was going on there. Feels as if . . . as if friends are fighting. I can almost hear sounds of battle. Almost. </b> The level of connection between them is just extraordinary.<br /><br /><b>Shadow is ever besieged, for that is its nature. Whilst darkness devours, and light steals. And so one sees shadow ever retreat to hidden places, only to return in the wake of the war between dark and light.<b></b><br /><br />House of Chains is an amazing read down to the last page. I quite enjoyed it and it's quite interesting how with each book the story get more intense.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15864985762441492080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1679415485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1679415485" />
    <a title="Jenna Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32846944-jenna-kathleen"><img alt="Jenna Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583785298p2/32846944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1679415485?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna Kathleen" href="/user/show/32846944-jenna-kathleen">Jenna Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553813135" href="/book/show/850962.House_of_Chains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32846944-jenna-kathleen?shelf=canadian-authors">canadian-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32846944-jenna-kathleen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32846944-jenna-kathleen?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679415485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17277198566354768929">Wow. Just when I was starting to think it couldn't get any better, it did.<br/><br/>After three Malazan books, I was accustomed to Erikson's writing style and his massive cast of characters whose perspectives change, seemingly, every other page. So, of course, to keep everyone on their toes, the format is totally different for the first book of House of Chains and we only follow one character: Karsa Orlong. Yet another character who has made it onto my ever-growing list of favourites. I could follow a who</span>
  <span id="freeText17277198566354768929" style="display:none">Wow. Just when I was starting to think it couldn't get any better, it did.<br /><br />After three Malazan books, I was accustomed to Erikson's writing style and his massive cast of characters whose perspectives change, seemingly, every other page. So, of course, to keep everyone on their toes, the format is totally different for the first book of House of Chains and we only follow one character: Karsa Orlong. Yet another character who has made it onto my ever-growing list of favourites. I could follow a whole separate side series of just Karsa Orlong, but for now, I will settle for the huge portion he is granted in House of Chains.<br /><br />In general, I found the plot moves quite slower throughout the book than the first three of the series, especially after "book one". The middle was not without its ups and downs, but on a whole, they were not as eventful as the middle sections of the previous installments. However, there are tons of great characters, new and old in HOC.<br /><br />The Rakaru storyline was well done. I loved all the scheming and the mystery, especially surrounding L'oric. It was interesting to see Sha'ik's struggle between <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ her identity as the goddess and Felisin. The few moments Felisin shined through gave great emotional depth to her character; in particular, the obsession she has with Tavore and her reflections on her sister  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />A new duo I ended up liking a lot was Pearl and Lostara. Both with their own agendas, wandering the desert.<br /><br />There was also a lot of old favourites I was glad to see: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Crokus, now Cutter, and Apsalar, Fiddler, and Kalam with short appearance by Quick Ben.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I loved watching them all doing their own separate thing.<br /><br />Cotillion was another great character with a large role, but not as much physical presence as some of the main characters. I was excited whenever he came in the main plot, and he's got his hands controlling quite a number of people so it will be interesting to see what he's up to.<br /><br />Of course, in typical Erikson fashion, the ending is what makes HOC really fantastic. I blew through 200 pages in one sitting because I just needed to know how events would unfold. It was just wonderfully done. A last minute appearance by <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Quick Ben to help Kalam and let him know the Brigdeburners have ascended: wow. The House of Chains is sanctioned and Karsa Orlong kicking ass - Bidithal's death was perfect. He deserved all of it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Then, after all the news and the awesome fighting displays, all of the sudden, there is an immediate drop in the tone. The duel was just so heartbreaking and now I need time to recover.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17277198566354768929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1891542879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1891542879" />
    <a title="Michael Britt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt"><img alt="Michael Britt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513347398p2/51188905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891542879?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Britt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Britt" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt">Michael Britt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51188905-michael-britt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891542879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11596606596626367342">"Raraku has swallowed more tears than can be imagined. Now comes the time for the Holy Dessert to weep"<br/><br/>This series is just way better than I could've ever imagined! Each book is great on it's own merits. While this one wasn't as exciting as Memories of Ice, it's still a 5 star book in it's own rights. The <i>only</i> thing I had a small problem with, at the time, was how the first quarter of the book was set up. But, I'm also very glad, looking back, that he did it that way. It set up a character that </span>
  <span id="freeText11596606596626367342" style="display:none">"Raraku has swallowed more tears than can be imagined. Now comes the time for the Holy Dessert to weep"<br /><br />This series is just way better than I could've ever imagined! Each book is great on it's own merits. While this one wasn't as exciting as Memories of Ice, it's still a 5 star book in it's own rights. The <i>only</i> thing I had a small problem with, at the time, was how the first quarter of the book was set up. But, I'm also very glad, looking back, that he did it that way. It set up a character that I'm so torn on how I feel about him. Karsa Orlong is the first character that I have both loved and hated at the same time. With characters like Felisin, I just couldn't stand her and only grew to tolerate her. But with Karsa, I hated him in the beginning and he really grew on me to the point where I would get goosebumps during his crazy scenes lol. I won't go into detail, but his revenge scenes near the end were just so perfect and epic. I still don't really like him as a person, but I absolutely love him as a character. <br /><br />The plot in this one was on par with the last 2 books, in my opinion. The pacing wasn't as fast, but I enjoyed it just as much. And it never got slow enough to the point of boredom, so that's a big positive. <br /><br />I did find the very end sequence, the last chapter, to be a bit underwhelming in how it was concluded, but after a few things happened and Pearl and Lostara came back, it redeemed itself. I'm not gonna lie, I may or may not have gotten choked up at a certain reunion at the end...lol. <br /><br />All-in-all, Erikson delivered yet another epic installment into the Malazan series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11596606596626367342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
