            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=desperado">desperado</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=entertaining">entertaining</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=hero">hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=br">br</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=killer">killer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1980636455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9841703393118149643">A great BR with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16037420-sade-agbaje' rel='nofollow noopener'>queen of Red Blades</a> and the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/41767362-jody' rel='nofollow noopener'>king of Claws</a>.<br/><br/>It’s my fourth adventure in Malazan and what can I say, I’m getting used to a load of characters and I know that my mind will be blown away again ;) <br/><br/>Characters. I enjoy the epicness and the fun I get watching the interaction among the characters. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>Braven Tooth! That bastard's still alive?'<br/> 'It was hard to tell at times,' Smiles muttered.<br/> 'Until his temper snapped,' Koryk added. 'Just ask Corporal Tarr there. Braven Tooth spent near </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText9841703393118149643" style="display:none">A great BR with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/16037420-sade-agbaje" rel="nofollow noopener">queen of Red Blades</a> and the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/41767362-jody" rel="nofollow noopener">king of Claws</a>.<br><br>It’s my fourth adventure in Malazan and what can I say, I’m getting used to a load of characters and I know that my mind will be blown away again ;) <br><br>Characters. I enjoy the epicness and the fun I get watching the interaction among the characters. <br><br><b>
  <i>Braven Tooth! That bastard's still alive?'<br> 'It was hard to tell at times,' Smiles muttered.<br> 'Until his temper snapped,' Koryk added. 'Just ask Corporal Tarr there. Braven Tooth spent near two bells pounding on him with a mace. Couldn't get past the shield.'<br> Strings glared at his new corporal. 'Where'd you learn that skill?'<br> The man shrugged. 'Don't know. Don't like getting hit.'<br> 'Well, do you ever counter-attack?'<br> Tarr frowned. 'Sure. When they're tired.'</i>
</b><br><br><br>I’m just amazed how this adds exciting and more believable spices to the characters. Just remembering Red Star’s and Gem’s or Pokeman’s and his missus interaction made me laugh again. <br><br><b>
  <i>'Hunts? What does she hunt?'<br>'Not what. Who. She hunts for me, of course.' His eyes glittered as he stared at Kalam. 'But has she found me? No! We've not seen each other for months! Hee hee!' He jutted his head closer. 'It's a perfect marriage. I've never been happier. You should try it.'<br>Kalam poured himself another cup. 'I need to eat—'<br>But Iskaral Pust was gone.<br>He looked around, bemused.<br>Sandalled feet approached from the corridor without, then a wild-haired old woman leapt in through the doorway. Dal Honese – not surprisingly. She was covered in cobwebs. She glared about. 'Where is he? He was here, wasn't he? I can smell him! The bastard was here!'<br>Kalam shrugged. 'Look, I'm hungry—'<br>'Do I look appetising?' she snapped. A quick, appraising glance at Kalam. 'Mind you, you do!'<br><br>You really don't know, do you?'<br>'Of course I don't!' he snapped.<br>'Then why didn't you just say so?'<br>'It was more fun conjecturing creatively, of course. How can a man be the object of a woman's interest if he's always confessing his ignorance?'<br>'You want me to be interested in you? Why didn't you say so? Now I will hang on your every word, of course. Shall I gaze adoringly into your eyes as well?'</i>
</b><br><br>Of course there is a more serious tone to the book, the fighting, the loss of dear ones, the drama of humanity. And if you think that serious stuff spoils the story, you are mistaken. It just offers the characters to do smth unexpected! And that is amazing :) <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494276225ra/22700173.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also it was interesting and cool to be introduced to a fresh new character, which was so unlike what I read in earlier books. It felt almost like reading Conn Iggulden and his book about Genghis Khan. I mean Kick Arse :) I must admit, I didn’t like him at first as he acted like a rude and ugly ogre, well, he changed not much, but these small changes made him more likable to me and at last I fell in love with him :) (I mean his kindness to dogs and to some of the characters) It seems that nobody and nothing can overpower or defeat him and that’s part of his charm as he knows that, but still cherishes the flashes of kindness. Can’t wait to see how he’d react when meeting some of other the great warriors or more of the gods :) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494274697i/22700022.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book offers the final countdown between two sisters, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Miss Whirlwind an Tavore. I must confess I hated Miss Whirlwind from the start, but I was eager to see what kind of person she became. I was a bit disappointed with her new role and POV as she wasn’t really active or scheming like a great master-mind, though the way the end sequence caught her essence, IDK......it was so well done, it touched my heart. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Trull Sengar is another great character, whose past greatly interests me. I’d like to know more about his kin and how his great rewarding relationship with Honor Act will turn the wheels in Malazan. <br><br>I was happy to meet the Chosen One and her beloved Knife <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cutter <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and of course a meeting with my Deadly Calm made my day. To my little disappointment they didn’t get full attention but when they did make appearances, they did it with style and great mystery. The love tension was thick and the insight and back-story into the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Throne of Shadow, Shadow-you-know-who, and Uncle Cotillion (I was amazed of his skill! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494276225ra/22700174.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> just proved the ability of the writer to create gripping story. <br><br>Heboric surprised me even more, I can’t wait to meet him every time as I know that I won’t expect the stuff I’ll get. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494274697ra/22700024.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I loved the scene when a certain warrior invited Gamet to join, it was so epic ❤ <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494274697ra/22700025.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Narrative. The story dives into relationships and actions that were committed in the previous books. I always say that I’m more into characters when reading, but to my mind Malazan has a really strong side of the story, too. Reading “House of Chains” I felt a strong pulling to “Deadhouse Gates”, not only continuing and explaining some threads of the characters, also it matched the plot geographically. Followed by horrible betrayals, great loses it is clear that this playdate in Malazan can’t take part without some emotional, historical and future regarding complications. Two fighting parties, every side with different preferences. It’s evident that both fighting sides seek revenge, and the war between these two armies is one of the best presented and most changing I’ve ever read. It’s nearly impossible for a reader to simply pick one side and hope they win as both sides are likable and flawy. I admit there’s not much exploration into warrens or new worlds, but I loved this one! <br><br><b>
  <i>’Most scholars, in their species-bound arrogance, believe that humans domesticated dogs, but it may well have been the other way round, at least to start.”<br>‘But those creatures aren't humans. They're not even Imass.'<br>'No, but they will be, one day. I've seen others, scampering on the edges of wolf packs. Standing upright gives them better vision, a valuable asset to complement the wolves' superior hearing and sense of smell. A formidable combination, but the wolves are the ones in charge. That will eventually change ... but not for those serving the Deragoth, I suspect.’</i>
</b><br><br>Lol, just think of this possibility :D <br><br>There was a dark side to the story, I mean Bidithal and his past time. Ugh, come on Erikson, leave the kids alone :O <br><br>To sum up, there’s no other series that can match Malazan in greatness, epicness and the stunned feeling I get after reading each book. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9841703393118149643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416454796?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416454796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6510407794983626963">I had high hopes for this book. It continues the story of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55401.Deadhouse_Gates__The_Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___2_' title='Deadhouse Gates (The Malazan Book of the Fallen, #2) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Deadhouse Gates</a> in the end of which a lot of people was really pissed off at Apocalypse rebels for slaughtering Coltaine's army thanks to betrayal on high level of command. Now that Adjunct's army came to Seven Cities, the possibility of revenge became real. This is what I hoped for. Well, the first mention of these people came in after 1/3 of the book. <br/><br/>So, what happens in the beginning? A new race is introduced best described as bloodthi</span>
  <span id="freeText6510407794983626963" style="display:none">I had high hopes for this book. It continues the story of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55401.Deadhouse_Gates__The_Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___2_" title="Deadhouse Gates (The Malazan Book of the Fallen, #2) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadhouse Gates</a> in the end of which a lot of people was really pissed off at Apocalypse rebels for slaughtering Coltaine's army thanks to betrayal on high level of command. Now that Adjunct's army came to Seven Cities, the possibility of revenge became real. This is what I hoped for. Well, the first mention of these people came in after 1/3 of the book. <br /><br />So, what happens in the beginning? A new race is introduced best described as bloodthirsty barbarians. Three young warriors from one of the tribes decided to have barbarian fun. I really could not relate to these guys as their idea of fun was to kill every single man/child and rape every single woman. Secondly, how come these three guys could slaughter entire villages full of warriors? Anyhow, their adventures take up about one third of the book. <br /><br />Once the plot came back to two opposing armies, things finally get really interesting. The only problem is that some of subplot ideas are back from the second book: a bunch of people are walking around in the desert for so long, both they and the reader forgot why are there in the first place. <br /><br />I also need to mention that this is the first Malazan book where I finally became confused and lost in the names of races, warrens, events, places, etc. - too much of these at once. <br /><br />Having said all of this, the last two thirds of the book are really good and make up for the slow start. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6510407794983626963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1293462556" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1293462556" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2613919-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483904179p2/2613919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1293462556?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/2613919-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8177008-house-of-chains">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1293462556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1751643398282170855">5 Stars <br/><br/>House of Chains deserves full marks for the sheer volume of action, changes, and actual size. This is a massive book, a long read, but funny thing is it never really felt like too much. This is a novel that you would have a tough time reading quickly and I feel that you might miss the point. House of Chains is a book to be experienced, at times quickly taking in the action and the wonderful world. At other times it should be taken slowly and carefully, allowing time to digest all that yo</span>
  <span id="freeText1751643398282170855" style="display:none">5 Stars <br /><br />House of Chains deserves full marks for the sheer volume of action, changes, and actual size. This is a massive book, a long read, but funny thing is it never really felt like too much. This is a novel that you would have a tough time reading quickly and I feel that you might miss the point. House of Chains is a book to be experienced, at times quickly taking in the action and the wonderful world. At other times it should be taken slowly and carefully, allowing time to digest all that you have experienced.<br /><br />As many others have said more eloquently, Erikson has created a fantasy world not to be missed. This book like the others sees many returning favorite characters and points of view. House of Chains does something unique in that the first 20% of this book follows one point of view, a new character named Karsa Orlong. Karsa is a larger than life angry barbarian like human that is not quite human. He steals the story in this book and is now one of my favorite characters. I was blown away by how much I enjoyed the focused writing of Erikson with just one point of view. I would love to read single POV'S by him.<br /><br />The overall story and plot of the whole series is in one word epic. I continue to be awed at just how much Erikson has going on and how incredible he weaves and minds each of the threads of this fantastical world. As I read more and more of this series I wonder if any other that I have read in the past will measure up. I love it.<br /><br />I had picked out several fantastic passages to quote but a Kindle crash seemed to have lost them for me. Needless to say House of Chains is the pinnacle of the series so far and it clearly demonstrates all that Erikson brings as a writer. There is a great deal of action, magic, and fighting. There are Gods, monsters, ghosts, and more. The story is dark, convoluted and deeply connected. It is simply AMAZING!<br /><br />My highest recommendations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1751643398282170855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s/gj++TU9TDUlhnS1iO5sENruoCJAAGQsVlSsfy6wzlh0hMJ0iEOw6vIBCCjR3lIYYzXw2wl3ln0tn+H48filg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LerNoDtCNziT+mHotJERardn/m/0vMF+fBSvt03kLR//wP1SDbfMy+ykfBrB9dGSlYCTLBGZHrc5+4KBUpkMsA==')})
  }
